Current Affairs Commentary

On the Hirota Cabinet

— He

Elder Statesman Saionji entered Kyoto upon imperial command and resided deep within the palace, consulting with Makino, Kiyoura, Yuasa, and others on the aftermath of the February 26th Incident. The results of their deliberations were nothing more than two points: first, "discipline the military" to maintain the national will; second, "international coordination" to appease the concerns of the financial circles. Such deep contemplation and long-term planning lead us to admire their appropriate handling of the situation. However, since the "September 18th Incident," the "Imperial Army" has been invariably victorious. The name "international coordination" is not only deeply resented by the military but even those who call themselves "graduates of Tsinghua," such as Konoe Fumimaro, cover their ears and turn away, respectfully declining the important task. Hirota Koki, a mere scholar relying on the demeanor of a diplomat, maneuvered between the financial circles and senior statesmen, suddenly gaining favor and rising to form a cabinet. The difficulties he faces are the opposite of those faced by Konoe, lying not in how to coordinate diplomacy but in whether the Miyakezaka can be persuaded to agree. Since the establishment of the "Cabinet Formation Headquarters," for several days now, he has been going back and forth, solely reliant on the military's breathing. This situation is truly unprecedented in the history of cabinet formation in Japan.

Nonaka Shiro and others, venting momentary anger, raised troops at the palace gates, alarming the Emperor and startling the people. The price they paid was merely the removal of Araki, Masaki, whom they most admired in life, and Abe of the "Ugaki faction," as well as Hayashi Senjuro, the leader of the "Ishikawa faction." However, Uetda Kenkichi and others of the Central faction reaped the benefits, rising prominently and uniting with the "Araki faction" that had not yet retreated from the Ministry of the Army. They forced Terauchi Hisaichi of the "Ugaki faction" to wield the weapon of the "Military Minister Ordinance" to engage in a fierce struggle with the representatives of the elder statesmen and senior ministers. Although this is not yet sufficient to overthrow Saionji's predetermined policy in one fell swoop, the initial blow was forceful and demanding. Hirota Koki, even with training from the Kokuryukai's Mitsuru Toyama, is likely to be frightened as a result.

This kind of legitimate tactic not only makes any cabinet appear to be difficult to produce but also foreshadows a future collapse. Today's Japan is nominally in a "state of emergency." The military demands the utmost exclusion of party members from serving as state ministers. Although the political parties have no choice but to temporarily accept this, with the leading Minseito party only gaining two seats under the "beautiful name of national unity," the power of the political parties still lies in the parliament. It is assessed that this will ultimately force Machida Chuji, the president of the party who holds the power to decide the budget, to rise up and overthrow the cabinet. Hirota, no matter how skilled, will likely become exhausted. This is the first reason. The army is demanding that Hirota pay an equal price for the "significant sacrifice of four generals retiring to the reserves." If this price involves diplomatic reversals of "international coordination" or financial abandonment of the policies of the late Finance Minister Takahashi, then Hirota will lose favor with the elder statesmen, senior ministers, and financial circles, and will find it difficult to stay in power for long. This is the second reason. This sudden upheaval occurred at the Emperor's side and was only quelled after several days, which is unprecedented in over a hundred years. The "disciplining of the military" by the elder statesmen and senior ministers can represent the demands of the national people. If Hirota cannot fully implement this or does so unsuccessfully, then successors to Nonaka Shiro will emerge in large numbers. This is the third reason. With these three points, the future political turmoil in Japan will likely resemble a raging wave that is impossible to approach. Can Hirota's "Japan Maru" avoid dangerous reefs as it pushes forward through the waves?

Hirota Accommodates Military Demands - New Japanese Cabinet Formed - Inauguration Ceremony Held Yesterday Afternoon - Seeking Thorough Strengthening of National Defense - Actively Advancing Mainland Policy

Tokyo - Hirota entered the palace at 7:00 PM to submit the list of new cabinet members, which was approved by the Emperor. The appointment ceremony for each member was held at 8:30 PM, and the new cabinet was officially established. (Ninth Dispatch from Reuters)

Tokyo - It is reported that Hirota has reached a compromise with the military on the selection of new cabinet members. Hirota will concurrently hold the position of Foreign Minister, Baba will serve as Finance Minister, and Raemo will serve as Minister of Commerce. (Ninth Dispatch from Reuters) A meeting was held at 9:15 this morning to discuss the military's demands, chaired by Hirota, with Terauchi, Nagano, and others in attendance. The differences of opinion arising from the military's demands are: 1. Hirota must formulate policies acceptable to the military, after which the military can recognize his cabinet. 2. The political parties must admit that they bear some responsibility for the February 26th Incident, because they only selected one member each from the Minseito and Seiyukai parties to join the cabinet. 3. Hirota has agreed that each party will occupy two positions in the new cabinet. 4. Hirota must formulate a national defense budget that is numerically acceptable to the military. Regarding this, Nagano firmly stated that naval expenditures may be greatly expanded, and asked for Hirota's approval. The meeting had not adjourned as of 12:30 PM. (Ninth Dispatch from Reuters)

Tokyo - Generals Terauchi and Nagano continued to meet with the leaders of the new cabinet at the Cabinet Formation Headquarters at 9:00 AM on the 9th. As a result of the negotiations, both sides reached a consensus, and the list of cabinet members has almost been finalized. Furthermore, a total of four members from political parties are participating in the cabinet, with each of the Minseito and Seiyukai parties sending two members. (Ninth Dispatch from Domei)

List of New Cabinet Members - Hirota Prime Minister Concurrently Serves as Foreign Minister

Tokyo - New Prime Minister Hirota entered the palace at 7:15 PM today to meet with the Emperor and present the list of cabinet members. Then, at 8:30 PM, the appointment ceremony was held with Interior Minister Goto attending, as follows: Prime Minister and Minister of Foreign Affairs: Hirota Koki; Minister of Interior and Minister of Education: Chao Huizhi-fu; Minister of Finance: Baba Yingichi; Minister of the Army: Terauchi Hisaichi; Minister of the Navy: Nagano Osami; Minister of Justice: Hayashi Raizaburo; Minister of Agriculture and Forestry: Shimada Toshio (Seiyukai); Minister of Commerce and Industry: Kawasaki Takukichi (Minseito); Minister of Communications: Raemoki Keikichi (Minseito); Minister of Railways: Maeda Yonezo (Seiyukai); Minister of Colonial Affairs: Nagata Hidejiro (Ninth Dispatch from Domei)

Tokyo - The brief biographies of the ministers participating in the Hirota Cabinet are as follows: Minister of Interior: Chao Huizhi-fu was born in Shimane Prefecture. He graduated from Tokyo University in the 40th year of the Meiji era. He served as a clerk in Nagano Prefecture and then as an official in the Ministry of Interior. He successively held important positions in the Ministry of Interior and was promoted to Director-General of the Ministry of Interior in the third year of the Showa era, holding the position until the eighth year of the Showa era. He is proficient in the affairs of the Ministry of Interior and is currently 56 years old. Minister of Finance: Baba Yingichi was born in Tokyo in the 12th year of the Meiji era. He graduated from Tokyo University in the 36th year of the Meiji era and entered the Ministry of Finance, serving as Director-General of the Tax Supervisory Bureau and then as Director-General of the Bureau of Legislation. He was awarded a Doctor of Laws degree in the ninth year of the Taisho era. In the second year of the Showa era, he was appointed as the President of the Japan Industrial Bank, a position he holds to this day. Minister of the Army: Terauchi Hisaichi is the son of the late General Terauchi Masatake. He was born in the 12th year of the Meiji era in Yamaguchi Prefecture. He graduated from the Army Military Academy in the 33rd year of the Meiji era and successively held important positions in the army. In August of the ninth year of the Showa era, he was appointed as the Commander of the Taiwan Army. In October of the tenth year of the Showa era, he was appointed as a General in the Army. It is rare for both father and son to have served as Minister of the Army. The General's nickname is "Bright General," and his nature is bright. His adjutant for three years said that he had never seen the General not be bright, but he is also known to be very strict about things.

Minister of the Navy: Nagano Osami was born in Tosa and is currently 56 years old. He graduated from the Naval Academy in the 33rd year of the Meiji era. He was appointed as a Vice Admiral in the second year of the Showa era and promoted to Admiral in the ninth year of the Showa era. He served as a staff officer of the Naval General Staff, Director-General of the Naval General Staff, Commander of the Yokosuka Naval District, Commander of the Fourth Fleet, and other important naval positions. He was also a plenipotentiary at the Geneva Disarmament Conference and was again appointed as a plenipotentiary representative at the London Naval Conference. He has a burly appearance and a clear mind, and is an outstanding figure in the Navy. Minister of Justice: Hayashi Raizaburo was born in Saitama Prefecture in the 11th year of the Meiji era. He graduated from the former Tokyo Law School (now Chuo University). He served as a judicial official in various locations and then as the Chief Prosecutor of the Yokohama District Court. He has served as the Chief Justice of the Supreme Court since May of last year. He came from a poor family, and his brothers supported each other and studied diligently, achieving what he is today. Minister of Agriculture and Forestry: Shimada Toshio was born in Shimane Prefecture and is 60 years old. He graduated from Tokyo University in the 33rd year of the Meiji era and became a lawyer. He was elected to the House of Representatives in the 45th year of the Meiji era and has been elected seven times since then, making him a prominent politician of the Seiyukai. He served as the Director-General of the Bureau of Legislation. Minister of Commerce and Industry: Kawasaki Takuo was born in Hiroshima in the 4th year of the Meiji era. After graduating from the German Law Department of Tokyo University, he entered the Ministry of Interior and served as the Mayor of Nagoya, the Director of the Police Bureau, the Director-General of the Ministry of Interior, the Director-General of the Bureau of Legislation, and the Chief Secretary of the Cabinet. He also served as the Secretary-General of the Minseito party. After the death of former Minister of Education Matsuda Genji, he succeeded him as Minister of Education. However, the cabinet was changed soon after the February 26th Incident, and he became a new cabinet member. Minister of Communications: Raemo Keikichi was born in Osaka in the 2nd year of the Keio era. He has been elected to the House of Representatives eight times since the 4th year of the Taisho era. He served as the Business Manager of the Yomiuri Shimbun and the President of the Imperial News Agency. He served as the Vice-Minister of Communications during the Wakatsuki Cabinet. Minister of Railways: Maeda Yonezo was born in Wakayama Prefecture and is 55 years old. He graduated from the Tokyo Law School in the 35th year of the Meiji era and became a lawyer. He has been elected to the House of Representatives seven times since the 6th year of the Taisho era. He served as the Director-General of the Bureau of Legislation and as the Minister of Commerce and Industry during the Inukai Cabinet. This is his second time entering the cabinet. Minister of Colonial Affairs: Nagata Hidejiro was born in Hyogo Prefecture and is 61 years old. He served as the Mayor of Tokyo twice, in the 2nd and 5th years of the Taisho era. He made great contributions to the reconstruction efforts after the Great Kanto Earthquake, which is a well-known fact. He is currently the President of Takushoku University, the President of the Imperial Education Association, and the Chairman of the Textbook Investigation Committee, as well as a member of the House of Peers. (Ninth Dispatch from Electric Communications)

Hirota Kōki Clarifies Cabinet Formation Policy

Tokyo – The cabinet formation headquarters, around 12 o'clock on the evening of the 8th, in the form of a statement by Premier Hirota, clarified its cabinet formation policy. The statement read: "The current domestic and international situation demands a new approach to past administrations. In order to adjust international relations, it is necessary to overcome the current extraordinary situation. We deeply feel that the cause of the current ominous events lies herein and are determined to implement a major reform. All political parties, the military, and bureaucrats should unite as a nation to eliminate long-standing abuses and establish a firm national policy. In selecting cabinet members, we will not be bound by past positions or duties, but will gather individuals who truly understand the current situation and possess a sincere dedication to serve the country to the death. After the government is formed, we will unite and strive to implement policies, upholding the Emperor's will and meeting the people's expectations, in order to cope with the severe situation," etc. (9th, Dōmei News)

Tokyo – Generals Terauchi and Nagano, on the afternoon of the 8th at the cabinet formation headquarters, held negotiations regarding important issues of the current situation, focusing on the military's written opinion. British Government Reaffirms Respect for Locarno Obligations: Willing to Thoroughly Study German Proposals to Rebuild the Foundation of European Peace; France Accuses Germany of Violating the Treaty Before the League of Nations

Full Text of the French Application Paris - Regarding Germany's abolition of the Locarno Treaty, the government recently submitted an application to the Secretary-General of the League of Nations, Aiwen, in the evening, and conveyed it to the Chairman of the Executive Yuan, Bruce, the Australian representative. The entire application is only one page and is typed. The content first states that Germany's dispatch of troops into the demilitarized zone along the Rhine River is a violation of Articles 42 and 43 of the Treaty of Versailles (ie, the provisions on the demilitarized zone) and Article 1 of the Locarno Treaty (ie, the provisions on respecting the demilitarized zone system). The country's unilateral abolition of the Locarno Convention is also a violation of the abolition procedure contained in Article 8 of the Treaty. According to the provisions of Article 8, the Locarno Convention should be invalidated by a two-thirds majority decision of the Executive Yuan of the League of Nations. As for the entry of German troops into the Rhineland demilitarized zone, although the country's government has provided assurances to the French ambassador that its meaning is "only symbolic," the actual number of troops is large and does not match the statement of symbolism. Now that the situation is urgent, it is necessary to take necessary measures to convene a meeting of the Executive Yuan as soon as possible to discuss this matter. This application was originally intended to be submitted jointly by France and Belgium, but in order to avoid delaying the time, France submitted it alone first, and the original text was sent to the Belgian government. Know that if there is a German soldier on the Rhine River, this alone is enough to prevent negotiations from taking place. I cannot consider the proposals put forward by German leader Hitler, for two reasons: Germany's unilateral abolition of the treaty has now been seen again (Germany abolished the military provisions of the Treaty of Versailles in March last year, which was the first time), and it is difficult to trust new proposals. Its intention is nothing more than to think that our political parties, whenever there is an election, often cause domestic disputes and disturbances due to differences in party views. The German government believes that this opportunity is worth taking advantage of, so the real reason why it took this decision by lightning speed is that I am going to engage in wall-gazing disputes. It is also known that in our country's history, whenever the country is in danger, all divergent party views can be immediately eliminated, and any political party will unite its aspirations in order to maintain national independence and protect national security. The German government had previously neglected this (referring to World War I), and is now repeating the same mistake. Someone on the other side of the Rhine River (referring to Germany) believes that some of our compatriots may be able to forgive Germany's actions in abolishing the treaty. In short, no matter who forgets to use France's internal divisions to achieve its goals, it will only see its efforts fail. In this situation, we, the French people, and international public opinion, should take a calm and prudent step in response to Germany with an attitude of loyalty and adherence to the treaty." Geography Lecture, Why Should We Learn Foreign Geography (Continued from March 1st)

— Professor Huang Guozhang, Department of Geography, National Central University

A third reason for studying foreign geography is that we can use the methods by which various countries adapt to their environments as a lesson for improving our own national economy and people's livelihood. Furthermore, the ways in which various countries around the world utilize their land can serve as a reference for improving our own land utilization methods. Improving our country's land utilization requires starting in two aspects: first, studying the conditions of our own country's land and its current utilization methods, which is a major purpose of our studying domestic geography; second, referring to foreign methods of land utilization to improve our own land utilization, which is what I am going to talk about now.

Why can we refer to and adopt foreign land utilization methods? This can be explained from two aspects:—

Land utilization methods vary from place to place – this can be explained by three points:

(1) Land utilization is closely related to the combination of natural environmental factors – the so-called natural environment is composed of various factors such as climate, topography, water systems, soil, mineral resources, natural vegetation, organisms, and their positional relationships with other places. There are no two places on Earth with exactly the same combination of natural environmental factors, but there are many similarities within the differences. Therefore, there are also many similarities in land utilization. For example, the rice-growing areas in China have many aspects that are exactly the same as the rice-growing areas in Annam, Siam, Japan, Korea, India, and Java. The United States, Canada, Argentina, Russia, and Australia are all wheat-producing regions with large exports, and they have many identical points in their land utilization methods. Furthermore, industrial areas such as those in eastern North America and western Europe have very little difference in land utilization.

In most places, land utilization is not limited to one method. Several different methods can be adopted on the same piece of land, and all can achieve reasonably good results. However, the methods adopted must have certain natural limitations. If the methods adopted are not suitable for the nature of the land, the result will still be failure. For example, the plains area of ​​the three northeastern provinces, although wheat, sorghum, millet, corn, and soybeans can be grown, and it can also be used for animal husbandry, it is not necessarily limited to one type of crop, but there are also certain limits. Not just any type can be grown. If rice and cotton are grown, there is little hope of success. In places with purely different natural environments, land utilization methods are also purely different. For example, in northwestern China, most of the land is sandy desert and semi-desert, with very little arable land. People live by nomadic herding, moving with the water and grass. There are few roads and sparse villages, all of which indicate a sparse population and a difficult livelihood. In the southeastern agricultural area, arable land covers the fields, roads are densely distributed, rural areas are everywhere, and cities are also very developed, all of which indicate a large population and vigorous vitality. Compared with most of the northwest, it is like two different worlds. Even within the southeastern agricultural area, the northeast is very different. The scenes in the cotton, wheat, and coarse grain area in the north and the rice, silk, and tea area in the south are clearly different, while the southwestern plateau area is very different from the northwest, and also has many differences from the southeast. Within the same country, land utilization methods are so inconsistent, so the disparity between countries is even more conceivable.

(2) Land utilization methods are related to the size and quality of the local population – suppose there are two places that can both develop agriculture, one with a sparse population and one with a dense population. In the sparsely populated area, it is more suitable to develop animal husbandry using its natural grassland than to develop agriculture. As for the densely populated area, of course, the development of agriculture is the priority. The rice-growing area along the Gulf of Mexico in the southern United States has a natural environment that is roughly similar to that of the Yangtze River basin in China. However, because the United States has few people and China has many people, one uses machines and the other uses manual labor, and their farming methods are completely different.

In addition to the number of people, the quality of the residents is also closely related to land utilization. The degree of technical knowledge that residents should have for various human occupations can make land utilization methods in two places with similar natural environments drastically different. For example, the residents of the desert and semi-desert areas in northwestern China move with the water and grass, and the products they produce are only enough to meet local needs; while the residents living in the desert and semi-desert areas in western United States and Australia adopt large-scale animal husbandry methods, using their products to supply the needs of the whole world, so that the living conditions of the people are very different from those in the northwestern region of China. In addition, the diligence and laziness of the residents, the level of living, social customs, and the quality of political organization all have a considerable impact on land utilization methods.

(3) Land utilization is related to a place's external relations – such as foreign trade, the types and lengths of transportation routes, foreign transportation equipment, financial and management institutions required for foreign trade, such as banks and import and export trading companies, as well as the size of government protection capabilities, such as the existence of unequal treaties, and whether protective tariffs can be implemented, all of which are sufficient to form the different characteristics of land utilization methods in various places.

Land utilization methods in various places are constantly changing – in very few places on Earth can people's land utilization methods remain unchanged for a considerable period of time. In places affected by Western material culture, land utilization methods can be said to change from generation to generation, or even from year to year. The original land utilization methods are closely related to the local natural environment, the size and quality of the residents, and external relations, and these are not fixed and can change at any time. In order to cope with the new environment, land utilization methods must change accordingly. Currently, our government is actively planning to use scientific methods to promote national economic construction, such as building railways, repairing highways, establishing steel plants, establishing air routes, improving crop seeds, improving livestock breeds, unifying currency, etc. These can make the environment in various provinces and regions change day by day. In order to adapt to these new changes, land utilization methods must also be improved from time to time. For example, the residents of southern Hunan do not currently have a railway going south to Guangzhou, and rely entirely on human, animal, and water power for transportation, so many rich resources above and below the land, such as forests and iron deposits, are difficult to develop due to inconvenient transportation. After the Changsha-Guangdong Railway is completed this October, although only a man-made route will be added to the environment of the residents of southern Hunan, the methods of land utilization by the residents must undergo many changes invisibly due to this route.

European countries are the initiators of scientific civilization, and many of their land utilization methods can be used as a reference for our country, especially those places whose environment is roughly the same as ours, which are even more worthy of our emulation. For example, the natural background of northeastern United States and northwestern Europe is the same as the Bohai Sea region in our country (including the Liao River basin in Northeast China and the provinces of Hebei, Chahar, Shanxi, and Shandong), which is a coal and iron-producing region with convenient transportation. Since European and American countries have been able to develop industries in these places, making them the heavy industrial center of the most important North Atlantic coastal region in the world, why can't our country use the Bohai Sea coast to create a heavy industrial center in the North Pacific region? If we had done this earlier, we would not have aroused the covetousness of other countries today. Not only can our country refer to the land utilization methods of other countries in the world, but other countries are also referring to each other. Now I will give three examples to illustrate this:

The methods currently used by Russia to develop Central Asia are the same as the methods used by Egypt to develop the lower Nile River, because both places are deserts, the sunshine and heat are very strong during the growing season, there are no drastic changes in air temperature, and there is convenient river water conservancy to supply irrigation needs. Egyptians can use the lower Nile River to grow cotton and become a famous cotton-producing area in the world, so Russians can of course use the same method to develop the land in Central Asia. After several years of efforts, the Russians have actually achieved great success. Many places in Ningxia, Gansu, and Xinjiang in northwestern China have not much different natural conditions from Central Asia. As long as we can build a railway from the interior to these places and improve their water conservancy to facilitate irrigation, I think we can definitely develop many good cotton fields and orchards to supply part of our needs. The cotton in Turpan, Xinjiang, is known for its excellent quality, and many parcels are mailed to Tianjin every year, which is enough to prove that the cotton planting industry in the northwest has great potential for development.

In the past, all the rubber used in the world was produced by Brazil in South America. Later, the uses of rubber expanded day by day, and the international demand increased day by day. Britain was unwilling to be controlled by Brazil and wanted to find places within its own territory that could produce rubber. As a result, it discovered that the natural environment of the Malay Peninsula was very similar to that of the Amazon River basin in Brazil. Therefore, it sowed Brazilian rubber seeds in the greenhouses of the London Botanical Garden, and then sent the rubber seedlings to the Malay Peninsula for cultivation. The result was very satisfactory. Later, the rubber industry spread from the Malay Peninsula to the Dutch East Indies, and now the Malay and Dutch East Indies have long become the world's main rubber-producing areas. Hainan Island in our country has a low-latitude climate and natural conditions very similar to those of Malay and Dutch East Indies. As long as it is used properly, it will definitely be possible to develop the rubber industry.

The natural conditions of the western United States and the northwestern part of our country are also very similar, and they are both pastoral areas. The US government specially sent the Roelich father and son to Inner Mongolia in the summer of last year to collect drought-resistant plant seeds to bring back for trial planting in order to improve the pastures on the western Great Plains.

The examples given above seem to focus on agriculture; in fact, it is necessary to refer to foreign countries for the development of various industries, and knowledge of foreign geography can be applied everywhere. To develop the manufacturing industry, it is necessary to understand the domestic situation, but at the same time, it is also necessary to understand the foreign situation. The raw materials and fuels required by the manufacturing industry are often not all supplied by the country and must be obtained from foreign countries. The nature and center of the manufacturing industry often depend on the supply situation of domestic and foreign raw materials and fuels. The same is true for the development of commerce. The commodity market is not necessarily limited to the country. The distance of foreign markets, the competition situation in various countries, and the external transportation routes are all sufficient for us to determine the nature and center of commerce, and this knowledge cannot be learned without studying foreign geography.

Finally, I will repeat and summarize again, we have three main reasons for studying foreign geography: first, we can understand the interrelationships between countries; second, we can understand the position of our country in the international community; third, we can use it as a lesson for improving the national economy and people's livelihood. (End)

Shanxi Province Implements Severing of Transportation to Bandit Areas

Shanxi troops are distributing proclamations to Communist Party members. Extensive communications and military deployments to suppress bandits by the Shanxi army are complete. Searches and suppressions are underway everywhere. The Shanxi Western armies, after recovering Sanquan Town in Fenyang County, are in high spirits and are advancing towards Zhongyang. Fierce battles are also ongoing in the Xi County area. Zhang Fufu, Deputy Director of the Central Training Directorate, Hou Cheng, Director of the Education Department of the General Staff Headquarters, and Gong Jicheng, Director of the General Affairs Department of the Ordnance Bureau of the Ministry of Military Affairs, arrived in Taiyuan from Nanjing the day before yesterday to visit the local authorities and inspect the latest actual situation in the bandit areas of Shanxi Province. They have been in daily consultation with local authorities and have telegraphed reports to the Central Government and Chairman Chiang Kai-shek. The Shanxi Provincial Government yesterday specifically stipulated measures to sever transportation to the bandit areas and ordered their immediate implementation. All Shanxi military commanders have issued proclamations to Communist soldiers, stipulating surrender procedures. The original texts of these measures are appended below:

Thirteen Articles of Measures for Shanxi Province to Investigate and Prohibit the Entry of Communist Party Members, Ordered to be Implemented by All Counties. The original text is as follows:

All border counties should designate a number of entry points on the border with neighboring provinces, assign personnel to set up checkpoints, and investigate pedestrians entering from other provinces. All other entry points are to be completely sealed off and not allowed to be used.

All pedestrians entering from other provinces must first apply to the county government or municipal public security bureau of their place of origin or place of employment for a permit to enter Shanxi or return to their hometown. The permit should state the reason for entry, prove that the person is not suspected of being a Communist Party member, and bear the person's photograph. The permit is to be presented to the checkpoint personnel for inspection, stamped, and then the person is allowed to pass. However, permits issued by the county governments or municipal public security bureaus in bandit areas are invalid.

When people from Shanxi Province return to the province, if they do not hold the permit mentioned in the previous article, they must obtain reliable proof according to the following regulations before they are allowed to enter: (A) Those serving in government offices must hold a passport or certificate from their employing agency; (B) Students must hold a certificate from the school they are attending or the head of their hometown street or village; (C) Merchants must hold a certificate from the chamber of commerce in their place of business or the head of their hometown street or village; (D) All other persons must hold a certificate from the head of their hometown street or village.

Anyone who does not hold the permit or certificate mentioned in the preceding two articles shall be prohibited from entering.

After entering the country with an entry permit or certificate, pedestrians traveling in counties implementing special passes should present their permits or certificates for verification and obtain a special pass.

If any engineering project in this province needs to recruit workers from other provinces, it should apply to the local government for a recruitment permit, recruit sufficient workers, and enter the country. The checkpoint inspection personnel at the border will check the number of people against the permit, stamp it, and allow them to pass. The permit will be verified and released along the way. After returning, the permit will be turned in and a list of workers will be prepared and reported for record.

All workers recruited in the preceding article must find a reliable guarantor to prove that they are not suspected of being Communist Party members. If any Communist Party members are mixed in, the recruiter shall be subject to joint and several punishment. After the workers are dismissed, the original employer should send them out of the province and report to the local government for record.

If any border county fails to thoroughly investigate and allow Communist Party members to sneak into the interior, the investigating county should inquire about the entry point and report it to the two provincial governments for verification. After verification, the county magistrate of the entering county and the responsible personnel under his jurisdiction shall be severely punished.

Any person or Bao Wei Tuan member who knows of Communist Party members sneaking into the country and reports them and they are apprehended shall be given a reward of one hundred yuan. The investigating government office shall strictly maintain the confidentiality of the aforementioned reporter.

Any border inspection personnel who take bribes to allow people to enter the country or extort and obstruct them shall be severely punished according to law.

The expenses required for each county to handle the investigation and prohibition of Communist Party members entering the country shall be reported for proper expenditure.

The inspection of pedestrians entering the country by large vehicles shall be handled jointly by personnel dispatched by the two provincial governments.

These measures shall be implemented from the date of issue. Fellow compatriots, the time has come for you to break away from the oppression of the Communist bandit leaders. What suffering is your life now? You are starving, you are freezing, you have no medicine for your injuries and illnesses, you walk barefoot, and you are forced by the bandit leaders every day to go against your conscience, burn villages, and kill people.

If you follow them to the end, you will still not avoid death. Can you endure this inhuman life? As for communism, your policy in the red area is only to concentrate land and food in the hands of a small number of bandit leaders. You will not get much of it. How can it be like the system of distribution according to labor advocated by Director Yan, where whoever works gets the fruits of their labor? This is fair. Your current actions can only destroy society and hinder evolution. What is the point? Speaking of life, we now eat white flour and wear warm clothes. You are starving and freezing, and you are about to starve to death. Why? Think carefully. Speaking of strength, we have cannons, machine guns, grenades, and the automatic help of the people. You are empty-handed and only fill the bandit leaders' eyes. You can only arouse hatred among the people. Why send yourself to death like this? Now you are violating the needs of the nation and deviating from the correct path of the Three Principles of the People. Your future will ultimately be annihilation. You are all citizens of the Republic of China. We forgive you very much. It is not worth it for you to die for the bandit leaders. Now is the time to defect. Wake up quickly and don't wait to die. We are giving the following to all of you:

Those who come over with a rifle will be rewarded with thirty yuan. Those who come over with a light machine gun will be rewarded with fifty yuan. Those who come over with a mortar will be rewarded with one hundred yuan. Those who come over with a heavy machine gun will be rewarded with five hundred yuan. Those who come over with a radio will be rewarded with one thousand yuan. Those who come over with other military equipment will also be generously rewarded.

Soldiers who come over and wish to serve in the military will be allowed to do so. Otherwise, we will provide travel expenses to return to their hometowns.

Officials of all levels who come over and wish to work will be given preferential employment. Otherwise, we will provide travel expenses to return to their hometowns. Signed, All Officers and Men of the Jin-Sui Army (Issued March 6th)

Dagukou's Ice Melts, Shipping Resumes

Shipping Merchants' Direct Losses Near Three Million; Tianjin Shipping Industry Cables Ministry Requesting Exemption from Tonnage Dues Tianjin Correspondence: The ice outside Dagukou has gradually melted and flowed out to sea due to the recent warmer weather and dramatic tides. Most of the ice near the Dagukou outer forts, Heigu, and the lightship has melted. Only the breakwater and the Dasan River area still have very thin ice, allowing large ships to pass without obstruction. The South and North ports are still mostly frozen due to wind direction and low water levels. As a result, the Dalian Company's Yijin Maru, the Sanbei Company's Sanxing, and the Zhengji Company's Fengli, which are frozen there, are unlikely to move within the next month or two due to the thick ice at the waterline. Fortunately, the ice in that area is like a plain, so the companies can hire workers to transport coal, water, and food to the ships so that the crew members do not starve. Inside Tanggu, the section of Xinhe and Gugu has some ice congestion again because the wind direction changed slightly in the afternoon of the 7th and that section is located at a bend in the river channel. On the 8th, the Changan Wheel, which was sailing from Tanggu, was blocked midway and specially telegraphed the Tianjin Shipping Company to request the Tianxing icebreaker for assistance. As of the 8th, in addition to the Tianjin-Shanghai route being unobstructed outside Dagukou, the routes between Yantai and Tianjin and between Dalian and Tianjin are still difficult to navigate due to the large amount of ice flowing from the Laotieshan area. All ships that were sailing have turned back midway. According to the observation of the shipping industry, it will take at least two weeks to return to normal. Currently, only three ships, Yijin Maru, etc., are trapped in the North and South ports. The rest have all escaped danger. Yesterday, the Yongheng ship arrived in Tianjin. The crew and passengers were trapped outside Dagukou for thirty-nine days. Food and fresh water were exhausted, and they had no choice but to eat the dried and fresh goods carried on the ship and drink snow water. They endured great hardship. After arriving in Tianjin, their hair was long and shaggy, and they were haggard, as if they had lived in another world. From the time the ice sealed Dagukou on January 10th, it lasted for more than fifty days. In February, eight ships entered and seven ships left Dagukou, and transportation was completely suspended. The total output for the entire month was more than 57 million tons, which is several times less than the 180 million tons of various goods exported when it was not blocked by ice. Although there are no statistics on the loss of customs revenue, it is estimated to be around four or five million. The shipping industry estimates that the loss of ships and goods can be roughly divided into (A) direct losses: 1. Loss of ship schedules: Averaging 500 yuan per day for large and small Chinese and foreign ships, the total loss is 1.5 million. 2. Loss of coal: 720,000. 3. Loss of food: 90,000. 4. Loss of boiler water: 20,000. 5. Loss of ship repair costs: 100,000. 6. Loss of public and private assistance fees: 150,000. 7. Loss of telegrams: 60,000. 8. Miscellaneous losses: 90,000. 9. Loss of 200,000 for 140 Tianjin port tugboats that have nothing to do for two months. The above nine items total 2.93 million. (B) Indirect losses: 1. Passenger losses cannot be statistically determined. 2. Losses of import and export goods can be divided into: Market price: 250,000. Freight: 100,000 (Ships cannot enter the port and are transported from other ports, which costs more freight). Damage (referring to destruction and remnants): approximately 120,000. Loss of interest: 200,000. Other losses of production, finance, and insurance companies are difficult to investigate at this time. The above indirect losses total 670,000. Among the various losses, the most severely affected are commodities such as coal merchants, rice, flour, groceries, fresh fruits, and cement. Tianjin shipping merchants are busy handling the aftermath. There are still many disputes involving both parties. What method will be adopted in the future to resolve them is also a matter of great study. On the 8th, the Tianjin shipping industry telegraphed the Ministry requesting an exemption from the tonnage dues of the trapped ships for the past two months to show compassion and sent letters to the Tianjin-Shanghai Shipping Association to provide assistance. The attached letters and telegrams are as follows: The Tianjin Shipping Industry Association's telegram to Yu, Acting Minister of Transportation, Ministry of Transportation, Nanjing: This sudden and unprecedented disaster in Dagukou has been rescued by you, and we are extremely grateful. Although shipping has been restored with great difficulty, the losses of shipping merchants during the ice disaster and suspension of shipping are enormous. It seems that tonnage dues should be exempted to show compassion and provide some compensation. Please consult with the Ministry of Finance and instruct the national customs to allow all ships that have suffered disasters to extend the validity period of their original tonnage dues by two months based on their disaster reports to show the great intention of the Ministry to protect national shipping. We urgently request that you approve this. The Tianjin Shipping Industry Association.

The Tianjin Shipping Industry Company's letter to the Shipping Industry Association: Dear Sirs, This sudden and unprecedented ice disaster in Dagukou has caused huge losses to the industry. Referring to the precedents of various countries helping shipping merchants who have encountered disasters, the government should provide relief. In addition to the previous telegram to the Ministry to find ways to provide relief, this association should also speak out for our shipping merchants and uphold justice. Please telegraph the Ministry again as soon as possible, consult with the Ministry of Finance, and instruct the national customs to allow all ships that have suffered disasters to extend the validity period of their original ship dues by two months based on their disaster reports to show compassion and provide some compensation. At the same time, please telegraph the Shanghai Association for assistance. Human effort can make a difference, and perhaps we can invite the government authorities to approve it. We are writing to suggest that you collect the consent of all member companies in writing and then send a telegram to the Ministry to achieve the goal. We hope for your support. Tianjin Shipping Industry Association Tianjin Shipping Industry Company's telegram to the Shanghai Shipping Industry Association: Shanghai Shipping Industry Association: This sudden disaster in Dagukou has caused huge losses to shipping merchants. This association has telegraphed the Ministry, consulted with the Ministry of Finance, and notified all customs offices to allow all ships that have suffered disasters to extend the validity period of their original ship dues by two months based on their disaster reports to show compassion and provide some compensation. Please telegraph the Ministry for assistance. We earnestly hope and look forward to your assistance. Tianjin Shipping Industry Association.

Japanese Military Attache Travels Deep into the Interior, Causing Anxiety Among the People of Chaozhou and Meizhou

Shantou Correspondence: Last month, Japanese Consulate Inspector Kakuda Susumu died suddenly on the road in Mingdeli, Qi Lu. This case has not yet been properly resolved. Since then, Japanese warships have been dispatched to patrol the Chaozhou, Shantou, and South China areas one after another. Japanese naval and military officers have come to Chaozhou and Shantou for inspection in droves, like carp crossing the river. General Matsui Iwane, who promoted the Greater East Asia Co-prosperity Sphere, persuaded the southwest authorities and passed through Shantou to Xiamen one day. Although he did not meet with Chaozhou and Shantou military and political officials, the captains of the Fuyong and Asagao, which are stationed in Shantou, and the president of the Japanese Residents Association held a grand welcome party. At the welcome banquet, they gave various important reports. After listening to these reports, Matsui contributed his strategy for dealing with South China, determined to promote the Greater East Asia Co-prosperity Sphere ideology, and accompanied this ideology with economic and diplomatic forces to penetrate the people of Chaozhou and Meizhou. After Matsui flew to Xiamen, Japanese Navy Commander Hosokawa, accompanied by Japanese Emperor's Military Attache Hirata, arrived in Shantou on the Yubari flagship. At that time, a rumbling cannon sound was emitted from the sea. Japanese Consul Tanaka, and more than ten important Japanese and Taiwanese people, including the president of the Residents Association, specially drove a motorboat to the Yubari to welcome them ashore. It is said that Hirata came to investigate the Kakuda case. Because of this, Li Hanhun, a member of the Eastern District Committee, happened to be taking the Haiheng ship to the province. Mayor Li Yuanhe was transferred to act as the magistrate of Shunde County, and Chen Tongchang, the former magistrate of Shunde County, was transferred to serve as the mayor of Shantou City. They were busy with the closing and handover procedures. Therefore, after Hirata and Hosokawa arrived in Shantou, they did not visit the Shantou civil and military authorities and returned to Magong Port in Taiwan on the Yubari warship at 5:30 p.m. In addition, the military attache of the Japanese Consulate General in Shamian, Guangzhou, Infantry Captain Taihei Hideo, and Artillery Captain Ogawa Kanji, stated to the provincial government through Consul General Kawasaka Tatsuo one day that they were going to travel to the Dongjiang area and requested that the military and police along the way provide protection. The Guangdong government was unable to refuse. Also, fearing that accidents might occur along the way, it specially sent a platoon leader of the military police, Liang Shiying, with six military police officers and six motorcycles to accompany and protect them along the way. Military attaches Taihei and Ogawa took a car on the Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway to Zhangmutou at noon on the 2nd, and then transferred to a provincial road car sent by the headquarters, and proceeded all the way. The weather has been cold and freezing for days, and drizzle has been falling. The provincial road trunk line has an uneven roadbed and is muddy and slippery. The Japanese military attaches do not mind the hardships of the journey and make a long journey in the cold wind and drizzle. They pay special attention to the scenery and terrain of the mountains and rivers wherever they pass. Even the small place names of the villages along the way are recorded in great detail. At 4:00 p.m. on the 2nd, they arrived at Huiyang City, turned to Pingshan and went to Haifeng. On the morning of the 3rd, they set off from Haifeng to Shanwei, and then turned back to Lufeng, Huilai to Puning. On the 4th, they entered Chaoyang via Liusha, and transferred to a steamer to Shantou. The people of Chaozhou and Meizhou are quite uneasy about the actions of the Japanese military attache.

General Situation of Hunan Province Construction, He Jian's Policies to Govern Hunan Are Generally Progressive in Various Aspects

Changsha Correspondence: Since He Jian has been in charge of military and civilian affairs in Hunan, he has achieved great results in both spiritual and material construction. He has always advocated using Confucian spiritual morality to engage in self-cultivation, family management, governance of the state, and bringing peace to the world, so that the inherent beautiful civilization can continue to illuminate the world. At the same time, he advocates adopting the new civilization of Europe and the United States so that China can also join the ranks of modern countries. Hunan Province is engaged in construction based on He Jian's proposals. Therefore, the education in the province excels other provinces in Chinese studies. There are more than 24,000 elementary and middle schools in the province. There is also Hunan First University established by the province. It is currently working to improve the rickshaw. Huang Shiheng, a provincial committee member, is appointed as the director to manage it. The provincial-level Zhongshan Library makes great efforts to preserve the ancient documents of the province. There are also Nanyue Library, Nanxuan Library, and Huda Library, etc., which collect famous ancient and modern works to benefit the people's intelligence. It strives to enable the people of the province to have a true understanding of both inherent culture and European and American civilization, so as not to make the mistake of treating precious jade as cheap and broken iron as precious. In terms of transportation, more than 3,000 kilometers of highways have been built, and more than 400 long-distance buses are in operation. There are more than 2,000 miles of long-distance telephone lines. Changsha City has established a wireless radio broadcasting station (1,000 watts), and more than 40 counties have installed radios, accounting for two-thirds of the province's area. There are more than 120 ships operating in various places. In terms of industry, there is the First Textile Factory and the Industrial Experiment Institute. The province is rich in various minerals, such as gold, silver, copper, iron, tin, lead, zinc, aluminum, mercury, bismuth, tungsten, manganese, sulfur, arsenic, crystal, mica, graphite, coal, petroleum, etc. There is a mineral chemical test institute and a geological survey institute. In addition, agricultural experiment fields, etc. are set up to seek agricultural improvement. The main foreign trade products are mineral sand and rice, followed by firecrackers, bristles, tung oil, and summer cloth. The art products are best known for Xiang embroidery, which is world-renowned. The entire Yuehan Railway is expected to be fully open to traffic in May or June, directly reaching Guangdong and Hong Kong. The highways and railways directly connecting Hunan to Yunnan, Guizhou, and Sichuan are also under construction. You can travel from Changsha to Nanchang, Jiangxi in the morning and arrive in the evening. The province's geographical location is actually in the transportation hub of the country. He Jian is rich in moral knowledge. He advocates that there should be a consolidated central government internally, and the establishment of national policies. He advocates international friendship and peace externally, and the realization of a world commonwealth through cultural cooperation. He believes that Chinese studies cannot only be limited to writing poetry and playing with words, but that all cultural relics, systems, and archaeology belong to it. If scientific methods are used to organize them, a new Chinese culture will be produced. He also advocates that China should advance from an agricultural country to an industrial country, so that there will be legitimate foreign trade to increase economic sources, enrich the national treasury, and avoid relying on domestic and foreign debts to make a living for a long time. The reason why Hunan Province has been able to achieve today's results is because the power is unified and there is ample time and opportunity for the rulers to engage in construction. However, Hunan Province has been disturbed by communist bandits in recent years, resulting in financial exhaustion. Seventy to eighty percent of the financial resources are spent on suppressing bandits. It is hoped that the communist bandits will be eliminated in the future, and all parties can understand and provide assistance, so that all construction will be even better.

Severe Cold Weather in Fuzhou Severely Affects Various Businesses, Many Poor People Die in the Streets

Fuzhou Correspondence: The Fujian Province is located on the southeast coast, and the climate is extremely warm. There is no severe heat in summer and no severe cold in winter. Even in the coldest months of December and January, the temperature in Fahrenheit is often above 50 degrees, and you can keep warm by wearing cotton clothes. Therefore, people's homes never have stoves, and ice and snow are even rarer. After the second half of February, you can wear lined clothes, and by the beginning of March, laborers wear single clothes. Even on the coldest days, the sun is extremely warm when it comes out. Therefore, there is a saying that beggars are not afraid of frost falling (because the sun will definitely come out if frost falls the night before), but they are afraid of prolonged rain (because prolonged rain will inevitably lead to floods and there will be no place to beg). But this year the climate has suddenly become abnormal. It is already the end of February and the beginning of March, which is the season when lined clothes are changed for single clothes, but it is extremely cold. The temperature in Fahrenheit has dropped to about 30 degrees, and there is continuous overcast rain, or occasional snow. Even if there is no rain, there are dark clouds and sunlight is faint. After 9:00 p.m. at night, there are no pedestrians on the road, and even at home, you can't keep warm without heavy fur coats and stoves. Because there is no one to watch the shows, the theaters often stop performing in the evenings. Only bathhouses are doing extremely well because bathing in hot springs can keep you warm. The most pitiful are beggars and rickshaw pullers. Most of these poor people do not have cotton clothes. Even if they do, they are broken and tattered. Most beggars sleep in the streets and alleys, under the eaves of temples. Most rickshaw pullers are addicted to opium (because the opium dens are all opened by Taiwanese people, and smoking is extremely free). Beggars have no place to beg when it rains, and they are even more hungry and cold from sleeping on the ground. Rickshaw pullers have few people going out because it is cold, and even if they do go out, they mostly take public buses to avoid the cold wind. Business is extremely bad. They have no money to smoke, and they can't pay the rent for the car, so they don't dare to return to the depot. Addiction and cold break out together, so many die. According to statistics, in the past ten days or so, an average of seven or eight beggars have died on the streets of the Confucian Temple, Nanmendou, Taijiangfan, Dasuocheng, and Shuibumen every day. Rickshaw pullers also die on the cars and on the roads every night. At the same time, many ordinary poor people steal to relieve their hunger and cold. Most of the stolen items are clothes and miscellaneous items, which can be taken to the private pawnshops opened by Taiwanese people to pawn. Only on March 3, a man named Chen Xima robbed Wu Xiangren, a bill collector from Meifu Company, of 4,000 yuan in front of the Feng Bank in Meiwu Ding, but he was unable to flee due to his frozen hands and feet, and was caught. He was sent to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation. According to his confession, his family was suffering from hunger and cold, and he was forced to do this. At the time, he thought there were only dozens of yuan, but he did not know that there was such a huge amount. Looking at his thin and haggard appearance, his clothes were ragged and tattered. He was shivering from the cold. Therefore, the prosecutors of the local court and the detectives of the Public Security Bureau have been very busy recently inspecting corpses found on the streets and arresting thieves. The Red Swastika Society and various charity groups have launched a shelter to accommodate poor and unemployed vagrants to prevent them from sleeping in the streets, and provide them with cotton clothes and rice porridge to keep them warm and relieve their hunger, so as to reduce theft. (March 7)

Songjiang, the Inspector-General Commissioner Will Arrive in Song on Schedule

Wang Gongyu, the Administrative Inspector-General Commissioner and District Security Commander of Songjiang District, is currently handling the handover in Tongshan. On the one hand, he has sent personnel to Songjiang to determine the location of the Public Education Hall as the office address. Yesterday, he sent Yang Fang and Zhou Jixian to Songjiang to arrange everything in the Public Education Hall office address. It is reported that the provincial government meeting has determined that the start-up fee is 500 yuan. Commissioner Wang is expected to arrive in Songjiang around the 14th to take office.

Aftermath of Damaged and Shut Down Machinery

The Songjiang Electric Power Company in this county suddenly damaged its machinery last night, resulting in the cessation of lighting for fifteen days in the section east of Ximen and west of Changqiao. It has reported to the county government for repairs. The county government has ordered the Public Security Bureau to pay attention to public security, and the First District Office has placed mast lights to hang in sections to facilitate pedestrians. However, transportation, postal and telecommunications, and prison agencies cannot be without electricity for a day. Now that part of the machinery is generating electricity, the Public Security Bureau has sent a letter to the company requesting that it hang lines and provide lighting for the above-mentioned agencies. It is not known whether it will be able to do so.

Administrative Commissioner's Office Moves to New Address

Zang Qifang, the Administrative Inspector-General Commissioner of Wuxi District, went to the provincial office to ask for instructions immediately after taking office on the 2nd of this month. Because the office building had not been determined for the time being, he temporarily set up an office at the local donation collection office. Later, the government officials determined that the Huangbu Gongye Public Office building was suitable and negotiated with Hua Shaochun, a member of the Commercial Committee, to rent it for 100 yuan per month. After reporting to Commissioner Zang, he moved to Wuxi the day before yesterday. Nie Dezhao, commander of the 7th Security Brigade of Suzhou, Shang Zonghan, commander of the 9th Brigade of Yushan, Yuan Qishan, commander of the 10th Brigade of Changshu, and Zhang Pinquan, commander of the 11th Brigade of Jiangyin, all came to Wuxi before the dike was breached to report on important defense affairs. At the same time, the county magistrates, secretaries, and public security chiefs of Jiangyin, Wujin, and Taicang counties came to Wuxi one after another to ask for instructions.

Silkworm Seed Production Volume in Jiangsu Province

In view of the serious shortage of silkworm seeds last year, which caused disputes, the Jiangsu Provincial Sericulture Improvement Management Committee specially ordered Zhou Wuxun, the chief technician of the Jiangsu Sericulture Experimental Field in Wuxi, to go to Japan for inspection, and jointly purchased spring seeds with Zhejiang Province, which have been shipped. Jiangsu Province has received a total of 30,000 sheets, which have been stored in the Luo Province Experimental Field for scheduled distribution. The total amount of spring seeds produced by various fields in the province is estimated to be more than 1.3 million sheets of raw seeds, equivalent to 1.1 million sheets of pure seeds. After deducting 400,000 sheets designated for Zhejiang Province, Jiangsu Province has a pure surplus of 700,000 sheets, which, together with the Japanese seeds purchased, is sufficient to meet the needs of this year's spring sericulture season.

Meeting of Tax Bureau Chiefs from Ten Counties in Wuxi

The Finance Department, in order to organize and increase the營業 tax revenue of various counties, specially arranged for Secretary Yao to convene a meeting of the營業 tax bureau chiefs from ten counties, including Zhenjiang, Jiangdu, Wujin, Wuxi, Jiangyin, Wuxian, Changshu, Kunshan, Tongshan, and Taixian, at Meiyuan in Wuxi the day before. They had practical discussions on both urging payment of old debts and increasing new revenue. Finally, it was decided that all collections would be made directly, without relying on trade associations to collect on their behalf. It was also decided that all would depart in ten days to implement thorough inspections to prevent concealment. After the meeting, the bureau chiefs visited the plum blossoms together and returned to their respective offices that evening.

Completion of the De Yuan Road

Government employees and teachers and students of this county implemented labor service to build the De Yuan Road, which began last month. Approximately 4,000 people participated, working in sections. As of the deadline, most of the earthwork for the entire road has been completed and the road surface will be paved soon.

Changshu: Additional Two Branch Lines for the Xihu Road

The Jiangsu Construction Department, in order to expand the Xihu Highway, plans to extend it north from Yangjian Station in the county to Fushan, naming it Yangfu Road. The Automobile Company, because the company suspected that the road was a specialized business built by the company, proposed to the Jiangsu Construction Department to proceed according to the original plan: starting from the east gate of this county, reaching Fushan, then extending northwest from Fushan to Twelve Bends, and connecting to the Chengxi Road. However, 建, eager to complete the highway network, approved the company's simultaneous progress. Changfu Road will be built by the Automobile Company, and Yangfu Road will be built by the Construction Department with hired labor. The surveying of both roads has been completed, and the roadbeds will be paved soon.

Call from Staff of Social Education Organizations

The social education organizations such as the people's education centers and stadiums in this county are ordered to close on the 15th of this month. All centers and fields have stopped working and are awaiting acceptance by the Education Bureau. However, there are many staff members in each center and field. Once closed, their contracts will not be completed, and they will feel financially insecure. Therefore, on the evening of the 8th, they had a dinner gathering at Shanjing Garden and unanimously decided to jointly submit a request to the Education Department to imitate the method of the Education Bureau's supervisors, to continue paying their original salaries during the training period of the directors and to pay the staff salaries until the end of the semester, in order to show consideration. They also expressed consistency with the attitudes of the counties of Suzhou and Wuxi.

Jiashan: Chairman Huang Arrives in Fengjing

Provincial Chairman Huang Shaohong arrived in Fengjing early on the 7th on his own boat for inspection, accompanied by four attendants carrying wooden-holstered guns. After arriving, he went to the Public Security Bureau for inspection, but the bureau chief was not in the bureau. He then went to the town office for inspection, but there was no one there. Finally, he inspected the highway engineering on the Hangfeng Highway. Huang considered Fengjing to be the gateway to the province of Wood, with an unusually important strategic position, so he attached great importance to it.

The Fenghuai Lawyers Association held its inaugural meeting at Jianghuai Middle School at 9 a.m. on the 8th. After the Completion of the Unified Government Bonds Printing, Exchange is Allowed Starting Tomorrow, Banking Association Announces Methods for Exchanging Bonds on Behalf of Clients, Central Bank Acts as Agent for Receiving Bonds and Prepares Bonds

After the issuance of 146 million yuan of unified government bonds, the printing was undertaken by the Zhonghua Book Company and has now been completed. Exchange will be allowed starting tomorrow. The Banking Association announced the methods for unified custody and mortgage clients to exchange bonds. The Central Bank announced preparations for receiving bonds and the methods for exchanging bonds. The details are recorded as follows:

Bond Exchange Starts Tomorrow

After the completion of the printing of the unified government bonds, types A, B, C, D, and E, the Ministry of Finance has stipulated that one type will be exchanged every ten days starting tomorrow. Now, the bond exchange office at 452 Jiangxi Road has received an order from the ministry and appointed personnel to handle the exchange. Starting tomorrow, the first type to be exchanged will be type A, which includes the Patriotic Treasury Bonds of the 22nd year, short-term treasury certificates, Customs Treasury Bonds of the 18th year, North China War Zone Government Bonds of the 22nd year, Security Bonds, and Customs Treasury Bonds of the 19th year. Those who went to the office to request application forms were very crowded. The exchange in other locations will be handled by the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and the Zhejiang Industrial Bank.

Banking Association Announces Unified Exchange

After the Banking Association resolved to unify the methods for various banks to exchange government bonds on behalf of custody and mortgage clients, Secretary-General Lin Kanghou has drafted the methods for exchange on behalf of others and sent them to various banks for consent. It is expected to be formally published in the newspaper today for the purpose of unification. The purpose is to facilitate clients who entrust custody and mortgages. It is stipulated that the receipts for bond custody and mortgages issued by various banks in the past should be exchanged for receipts for new government bonds at various banks within two weeks after the Ministry of Finance announced the exchange date for various bonds.

Central Bank Announces Exchange on Behalf of Clients

Yesterday, the Issuing Bureau of the Central Bank sent letters to various banks and money shops that receive bonds, saying: "Regarding your bank/shop's various bonds under the item of guarantee preparation for receiving bonds in our bureau, we now intend to handle the procedures for exchanging for unified government bonds in accordance with the provisions of the Ministry of Finance's Announcements No. 132 and No. 133, which will be handled by our bureau on your behalf. However, each sheet must be stamped. It is stipulated that every 50 sheets of each type of bond should be bound into one roll and sealed. If there are fewer than 50 sheets, each sheet must still be stamped individually. Please send personnel to the bureau from March 9th to handle the exchange procedures (the exchange in other locations will be handled entirely by our bureau on your behalf). After the exchange procedures are completed, within two weeks, bring the original receipt to the bureau for endorsement. After all the exchanges are completed, the receipt will be replaced. Checking the procedures for organizing and exchanging new bonds is very complicated. Starting from today, the temporary transfer and exchange will be suspended. Please note accordingly."

YMCA Fundraising Assembly Opens, Mayor Wu Gives Earnest Speech

The 36th Fundraising Assembly of the YMCA, led by Captain Wu Tiecheng, the mayor, yesterday invited the captains and members of the 60 teams and the donation committee members to a dinner at the International Hotel on Jing'an Temple Road and held an opening ceremony. More than 400 people attended, full of vigor and spirit, which was unprecedented in previous fundraising assemblies. During the meeting, Mayor Wu first gave an opening speech, followed by a dismissal. The details are recorded separately as follows:

Attendance: Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Wang Zhengting, Zhao Jinqing, Wang Xiaoxiang, Li Zhaohuan, Qian Xinzhi, Wang Yansong, Guo Shun, Yun Xiang, Shen Siliang, Zheng Xitao, Guo Chengwen, Wang Boqi, Chen Heqin, Cai Jinjun, Pan Lun, Xu Peihuang, Pei Zhenhuan, Wang Zhengxu, Bian Yuying, Lu Meiseng, Zhuo, Zhang Shangzhen, Kechang, Zhuang Yunqing, Xian Zhizhong, Liang Xiaochu, Chen Nengfang, Qian Huafu, Zhang Mingqin, and more than 400 other people.

Mayor's Speech: "Today is the opening ceremony of the 36th Fundraising Assembly of the Shanghai YMCA. I am very pleased to invite all the team leaders and members to gather together for a meal. This time, the organization and fundraising efforts are divided into 60 teams, plus 10 junior teams and 120 donation committee members. In total, there are more than 800 people participating in this fundraising effort. The goal is to have 5,000 members, 60,000 shares of membership fees, and 20,000 yuan in donations, for a total of 80,000 yuan. Based on the experience of the past two years and the efforts of everyone, we can be confident that the results of this fundraising assembly will not only achieve the goal, but will also break the previous records. We remember that in the ninth year of the Republic of China, when the National Congress of the YMCA was held in Guangzhou, Premier Sun gave a speech to the representatives, in which he said, 'If we want to create a good country, we must first have good character in everyone. Among all of us in China, those who have complete character are the YMCA.' This is Premier Sun's most alerting, simplest, and most descriptive sentence about the purpose of the YMCA. Now the people of the country are crying out for national salvation. In many places, they are not only crying out, but are already directly and indirectly doing the work of saving the country. Among this work, what is the most difficult and fundamental? It is to establish the Republic of China, so that the Chinese nation can achieve equality and freedom in the world. But according to Premier Sun's instructions, if we want to build a good country, we must first have good character, so we must know whether our country can be saved and whether our nation can achieve equality and freedom depends on whether the character of our nation is sound. Premier Sun said, 'Those who have character are the YMCA. It does not mean that there are no organizations with character besides the YMCA, because the YMCA is entirely based on promoting character as its purpose, and it can create complete character. The Chinese people's interpretation of the word character is often too narrow. In the past, people generally thought that being upright, not being corrupt, and not doing bad things meant having good character. But this interpretation is not in line with the present era, because ancient society and life were simple, while modern society and life are complex. It was easy to be a good person in the past, but it is difficult to be a good person now. Modern people must cope with modern society and achieve the purpose of survival, so the components of modern character are not just passively being a person. Just having noble morals is not enough for complete character. It also requires knowledge and ability. Only a person with all kinds of character is complete, a good citizen, and can build a good country. Therefore, the previous passive character was only about cultivating oneself. The current active character must also benefit the world. This kind of active character cannot be created only in the family or in school. It must be combined in all aspects. The YMCA's purpose is to create this kind of character, so the YMCA is a social and moral organization. It is not just talking, but also working hard. Since the YMCA is a social organization, everyone should work hard to maintain and help it follow this path together, seek to build the country, and revitalize the nation. Therefore, the whole society must be mobilized to help this fundraising assembly. On the one hand, it is fundraising, and on the other hand, it can measure whether the society sympathizes with the work done by the YMCA. There are 800 people participating in this fundraising assembly, such a great force, active in one month, I think that with your faith and enthusiasm, the impact will be great. That is why I am confident that this fundraising assembly can succeed. I wish this victory in advance."

Wang Rutang's Speech: "Today's opening ceremony of the 36th Fundraising Assembly of the YMCA is a good sign with so many people participating. I have four meanings for the YMCA: 1. The YMCA is always charging forward. Sports, hygiene, and other things were initially promoted by the YMCA, and now they have become popular. 2. The YMCA comrades are always working hard. For example, last year's fundraising was in a bad economic situation, but it was still able to exceed the goal. 3. The YMCA comrades can continue to serve continuously. Dr. 鄘富灼 served as the president for 13 years and is still a director. 4. Shanghai is a big city in the country. The YMCA in Shanghai not only serves the Shanghai community, but can also be a model for the whole country. This year's fundraising assembly has such a spirit and will surely achieve its goal. I hope this spirit will be maintained forever and continue to benefit the society and the country."

Gate North Wood Merchants Follow Advice to Resume Business, Manager of Futai Wood Firm Has Filed Private Prosecution, Finance Bureau Has Set a Proper Solution

More than ten wood firms in Gate North Guangfu Road, including Yuanxing, Fuji, Xiesheng, Hengxiang, Futai, Ruida, Dachang, Zida, Yuanshun, Yongda, Dafeng, and Xiangmao, jointly stopped business on the 6th of this month to protest the Finance Bureau's Gate North Inspection Department's additional rent tax and the detention of the manager of Futai Wood Firm. They also petitioned various agencies. After the City Party Department, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and other organizations persuaded them, the Timber Industry Association announced the day before that they would resume business first and wait for a solution. Yesterday morning, the wood firms along Guangfu Road followed the advice and resumed business. Signs with the words "Following the advice of the City Party Department and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, we will resume business first and wait for a solution" were posted at the entrances. As for the case of the manager of Futai Wood Firm, Chen Hongzhang, who was pursued for unpaid taxes, he has entrusted lawyer Xu Zuoliang to file a private prosecution with the court. China-Japan Wireless Telephone: Expanded Coverage Begins Today, Major Japanese Cities Can Now Connect with Shanghai

After China and Japan established wireless telephone communication, it felt as if being in the same room despite the vast ocean separating them. Merchants and citizens of both countries praised its convenience. However, the communication area was limited only to Shanghai and Tokyo. Previously, the Ministry of Communications, in order to expand the China-Japan wireless telephone communication area, instructed the relevant authorities in this city to actively prepare for it. Originally, it was planned to be implemented starting from the 5th of this month, but it did not materialize due to insufficient preparation. It is now learned that the expansion of the China-Japan wireless telephone communication area: the relevant authorities in this city have received a notice from Tokyo that 170 cities across Japan, including Osaka, Kobe, and Yokohama, which have the necessary equipment, can now fully communicate starting today.
